The requirement about handling lazy translation objects suggests we need to evaluate them first, but then we still need to respect whether the evaluated result is a protected type and shouldn't be escaped.\n\nLooking at `conditional_escape`, it already handles Promise objects by converting them to strings before checking for `__html__`. So the original approach should work: call `force_str` with the specified encoding and `strings_only` parameter, then apply `conditional_escape` to handle lazy objects and SafeData. The check for protected types only matters when `strings_only=True`, since `force_str` won't return a protected type otherwise.\n\nThe implementation is straightforward: convert the text using `force_str` with the given encoding parameters, then pass it through `conditional_escape` to safely handle HTML escaping while preserving already-safe content. When `strings_only=True`, protected types like integers or decimals bypass both conversion and escaping entirely. escaping\n    if is_protected_type(text):\n        return text\n    \n    # Otherwise, apply conditional escaping (handles lazy objects and SafeData)\n    return conditional_escape(text)\n\nThe logic handles different input types correctly. When strings_only=False and the input is a number like 123, it converts to \"123\" and escapes normally. When strings_only=True with a number, force_str returns the original value, which is identified as a protected type and returned unchanged. For string inputs with strings_only=True, the string gets converted and then checked—if it's marked as safe, it bypasses escaping; otherwise it gets escaped.\n\nThe approach is solid, so I'll move forward with this implementation. I could simplify further by relying on force_str's behavior with strings_only, but the current structure is already clean. This prevents bugs where developers forget a step or apply them\n    in the wrong order.\n\n    Parameters:\n    - text: The input to be converted and escaped (bytes, str, or other types)\n    - encoding: The encoding to use when decoding bytes (default: \"utf-8\")\n    - errors: How to handle encoding errors (default: \"strict\")\n    - strings_only: If True, protected types (int, float, Decimal, datetime,\n      etc.) are returned as-is without conversion or escaping (default: False)\n\n    Returns:\n    - A SafeString object containing HTML-escaped text, or a protected type\n      if strings_only=True and the input is a protected type\n\n    Examples:\n    - escape_with_encoding(b'caf\\xe9') -> 'café'\n    - escape_with_encoding('<script>') -> '&lt;script&gt;'\n    - escape_with_encoding(b'<tag>', encoding='latin-1') -> '&lt;tag&gt;'\n    - escape_with_encoding(123, strings_only=True) -> 123 (unchanged)\n    \"\"\"\n    from django.utils.encoding import force_str, is_protected_type\n\n    #
